<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Abortion</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Termination of a pregnancy</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Abortion_(disambiguation)" title="Abortion (disambiguation)">Abortion (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output rel="nofollow">007382</a></span></td></tr><tr class="noprint"><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div style="text-align: right;">[<a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q8452" title="d:Q8452">edit on Wikidata</a>]</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Abortion</b> is the termination of a <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a> by removal or expulsion of an <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fetus" title="Fetus">fetus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[nb 1]</a></sup> An abortion that occurs without intervention is known as a <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a> or "spontaneous abortion"; these occur in approximately 30% to 40% of pregnancies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-John2012_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-John2012-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2013Epi_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2013Epi-4">[3]</a></sup> When deliberate steps are taken to end a pregnancy, it is called an <a href="#Induced">induced abortion</a>, or less frequently "induced miscarriage". The unmodified word <i>abortion</i> generally refers to an induced abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> The reasons why women have abortions are diverse and vary across the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guttmacher_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-guttmacher-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bankole98_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-bankole98-8">[7]</a></sup> Reasons include <a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">maternal health</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guttmacher_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-guttmacher-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bankole98_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-bankole98-8">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">an inability to afford a child</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, lack of support, feeling they are too young, wishing to complete education or advance a career,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-9">[8]</a></sup> and not being able or willing to raise a child conceived as a result of <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> or <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bankole98_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-bankole98-8">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>When properly done, induced abortion is <a href="#Safety">one of the safest procedures in medicine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-grimes_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-lancet-grimes-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">: <span class="tooltip tooltip-dashed" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed;" title='Page: 1
Quotation : "Unsafe abortion is a persistent, preventable pandemic. ... By contrast, legal abortion in industrialised nations has emerged as one of the safest procedures in contemporary medical practice, with minimum morbidity and a negligible risk of death."'>1</span> </sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ray2014_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ray2014-11">[10]</a></sup> In the United States, the risk of maternal mortality is 14 times lower after induced abortion than after childbirth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimes2012_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grimes2012-12">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">Unsafe abortions</a>—those performed by people lacking the necessary skills, or in inadequately resourced settings—are a major cause of <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal death</a>, especially in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">developing world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO-preventing-unsafe_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-preventing-unsafe-13">[12]</a></sup> though self-managed medication abortions are highly effective and safe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Public health data shows that making safe abortion legal and accessible reduces maternal deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Modern methods use <a href="/wiki/Medical_abortion" title="Medical abortion">medication</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surgical_abortion" title="Surgical abortion">surgery</a> for abortions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[17]</a></sup> The drug <a href="/wiki/Mifepristone" title="Mifepristone">mifepristone</a> in combination with <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin" title="Prostaglandin">prostaglandin</a> appears to be as safe and effective as surgery during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_trimester" title="First trimester">first</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_trimester" title="Second trimester">second trimester</a> of pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kapp2013_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kapp2013-19">[18]</a></sup> The most common surgical technique involves <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_evacuation" title="Dilation and evacuation">dilating</a> the <a href="/wiki/Cervix" title="Cervix">cervix</a> and using a <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_aspiration" title="Vacuum aspiration">suction device</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">Birth control</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Combined oral contraceptive pill">the pill</a> or <a href="/wiki/Intrauterine_device" title="Intrauterine device">intrauterine devices</a>, can be used immediately following abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kapp2013_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kapp2013-19">[18]</a></sup> When performed legally and safely on a woman who desires it, induced abortions do not increase the risk of long-term <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental</a> or physical problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2014_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2014-21">[20]</a></sup> In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">unsafe abortions</a> performed by unskilled individuals, with hazardous equipment, or in unsanitary facilities cause 47,000 deaths and 5 million hospital admissions each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2014_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2014-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBGY09_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-OBGY09-22">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> states that "access to legal, safe and comprehensive abortion care, including <a href="/wiki/Post-abortion_care" title="Post-abortion care">post-abortion care</a>, is essential for the attainment of the highest possible level of sexual and reproductive health".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 73 million abortions are performed each year in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> with about 45% done unsafely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Abortion rates changed little between 2003 and 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup> before which they decreased for at least two decades as access to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> and birth control increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldtrends2007_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldtrends2007-27">[26]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Abortion&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 37% of the world's women had access to legal abortions without limits as to reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gutt_2018_fact_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gutt_2018_fact-28">[27]</a></sup> Countries that permit abortions have different limits on how late in pregnancy abortion is allowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJGO10_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-IJGO10-29">[28]</a></sup> Abortion rates are similar between countries that ban abortion and countries that allow it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/History_of_abortion" title="History of abortion">Historically</a>, abortions have been attempted using <a href="/wiki/Abortifacient" title="Abortifacient">herbal medicines</a>, sharp tools, <a href="/wiki/Fundal_massage" title="Fundal massage">forceful massage</a>, or through other <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional methods</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Management_of_Abortion,_Chp_1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Management_of_Abortion,_Chp_1-31">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abortion_law" title="Abortion law">Abortion laws</a> and cultural or religious views of abortions are different around the world. In some areas, abortion is legal only in specific cases such as rape, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fetal_defects" title="Fetal defects">fetal defects</a>, poverty, risk to a woman's health, or incest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dev98-07_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dev98-07-32">[31]</a></sup> There is <a href="/wiki/Abortion_debate" title="Abortion debate">debate</a> over the moral, ethical, and legal issues of abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> Those who <a href="/wiki/Anti-abortion_movements" title="Anti-abortion movements">oppose abortion</a> often argue that an embryo or fetus is a person with a <a href="/wiki/Right_to_life" title="Right to life">right to life</a>, and thus equate abortion with <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> Those who <a href="/wiki/Abortion-rights_movements" title="Abortion-rights movements">support the legality of abortion</a> often argue that it is part of a <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">woman's right to make decisions about her own body</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> Others favor legal and accessible abortion as a public health measure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Induced">Induced</span></h3>
<p>Approximately 205 million pregnancies occur each year worldwide. Over a third are <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">unintended</a> and about a fifth end in induced abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Most abortions result from unintended pregnancies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, 1 to 2% of abortions are done due to genetic problems in the fetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2014_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2014-21">[20]</a></sup> A pregnancy can be intentionally aborted in several ways. The manner selected often depends upon the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embryonic_age" title="Embryonic age">gestational age</a> of the embryo or fetus, which increases in size as the pregnancy progresses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Specific procedures may also be selected due to legality, regional availability, and doctor or a woman's personal preference.
</p><p>Reasons for procuring induced abortions are typically characterized as either therapeutic or elective. An abortion is medically referred to as a therapeutic abortion when it is performed to save the life of the pregnant woman; to prevent harm to the woman's <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">physical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a>; to terminate a pregnancy where indications are that the child will have a significantly increased chance of mortality or morbidity; or to <a href="/wiki/Selective_reduction" title="Selective reduction">selectively reduce</a> the number of fetuses to lessen health risks associated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_pregnancy" title="Multiple pregnancy">multiple pregnancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roche1_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-roche1-44">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6-45">[44]</a></sup> An abortion is referred to as an elective or voluntary abortion when it is performed at the request of the woman for non-medical reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6-45">[44]</a></sup> Confusion sometimes arises over the term "elective" because "<a href="/wiki/Elective_surgery" title="Elective surgery">elective surgery</a>" generally refers to all scheduled surgery, whether medically necessary or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eos-elective_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-eos-elective-46">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spontaneous">Spontaneous</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">Miscarriage</a></div>
<p>Miscarriage, also known as spontaneous abortion, is the unintentional expulsion of an embryo or fetus before the 24th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestational_age_(obstetrics)" title="Gestational age (obstetrics)">week of gestation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> A pregnancy that ends before 37 weeks of gestation resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Live_birth_(human)" title="Live birth (human)">live-born</a> infant is a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premature_birth" title="Premature birth">premature birth</a>" or a "preterm birth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> When a fetus dies <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">in utero</a> after <a href="/wiki/Fetal_viability" title="Fetal viability">viability</a>, or during <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">delivery</a>, it is usually termed "<a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">stillborn</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premature_births" title="Premature births">Premature births</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">stillbirths</a> are generally not considered to be miscarriages, although usage of these terms can sometimes overlap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies of pregnant women in the US and China have shown that between 40% and 60% of embryos do not progress to birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gabbe,_Chp_24_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gabbe,_Chp_24-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The vast majority of miscarriages occur before the woman is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinically_silent" title="Clinically silent">aware that she is pregnant</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6-45">[44]</a></sup> and many pregnancies spontaneously abort before medical practitioners can detect an embryo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Between 15% and 30% of known pregnancies end in clinically apparent miscarriage, depending upon the age and health of the pregnant woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> 80% of these spontaneous abortions happen in the first trimester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams18_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams18-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most common cause of spontaneous abortion during the first trimester is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chromosomal_abnormalities" title="Chromosomal abnormalities">chromosomal abnormalities</a> of the embryo or fetus,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_Gyn,_Chp_6-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mednet_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-mednet-57">[56]</a></sup> accounting for at least 50% of sampled early pregnancy losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fetal_med_837_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-fetal_med_837-58">[57]</a></sup> Other causes include <a href="/wiki/Vascular_disease" title="Vascular disease">vascular disease</a> (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">lupus</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes</a>, other <a href="/wiki/Endocrine_disease" title="Endocrine disease">hormonal problems</a>, infection, and abnormalities of the uterus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mednet_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-mednet-57">[56]</a></sup> Advancing maternal age and a woman's history of previous spontaneous abortions are the two leading factors associated with a greater risk of spontaneous abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fetal_med_837_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-fetal_med_837-58">[57]</a></sup> A spontaneous abortion can also be caused by accidental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_trauma" title="Physical trauma">trauma</a>; intentional trauma or stress to cause miscarriage is considered induced abortion or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feticide" title="Feticide">feticide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fetal_Homicide_Laws_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fetal_Homicide_Laws-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">Methods</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical">Medical</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medical_abortion" title="Medical abortion">Medical abortion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><div class="image"><div class="thumbimage" style="width:300;height:;font-size:80%;"><div style="position:relative;text-align:center;top:0;left:0;width:300px;height:190px;"><div style="position:absolute;top:0%;bottom:0%;left:30%;right:70%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px 0px 0px 1px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:white;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"> </div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:0%;bottom:0%;left:70%;right:30%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px 0px 0px 1px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:white;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"> </div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:0%;bottom:88%;left:0%;right:0%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#ffbcd8;"><div title="Manual vacuum aspiration">MVA</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:19%;bottom:71%;left:40%;right:35%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div style="position:absolute;top:38%;bottom:52%;left:15%;right:70%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div abortion">Hyst.</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:56%;bottom:34%;left:15%;right:62.5%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div curettage">D&amp;C</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:56%;bottom:34%;left:50%;right:25%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"><a href="/wiki/Intact_dilation_and_extraction" title="Intact dilation and extraction">Intact D&amp;X</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:74%;bottom:16%;left:7.5%;right:70%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div title="Mifepristone">Mifepr.</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:74%;bottom:16%;left:40%;right:25%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#bdc9df;"><div style="position:absolute;top:90%;bottom:0%;left:0%;right:70%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#b7e690;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_trimester" title="First trimester">0–12 wks</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:90%;bottom:0%;left:30%;right:30%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#dfe988;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_trimester" title="Second trimester">12–28 weeks</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:90%;bottom:0%;left:70%;right:0%;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;border-color:#cccccc;color:black;background-color:#e9c788;"><div style="position:absolute;left:0%;top:0%;width:100%;height:100%;display:table;"><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_trimester" title="Third trimester">28–40 wks</a></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption">
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestational_age_(obstetrics)" title="Gestational age (obstetrics)">Gestational age</a> may determine which abortion methods are practiced.</div></div></div>
<p>Medical abortions are those induced by <a href="/wiki/Abortifacient" title="Abortifacient">abortifacient</a> pharmaceuticals. Medical abortion became an alternative method of abortion with the availability of <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin" title="Prostaglandin">prostaglandin</a> <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin_analogue" title="Prostaglandin analogue">analogs</a> in the 1970s and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiprogestin" title="Antiprogestin">antiprogestogen</a> <a href="/wiki/Mifepristone" title="Mifepristone">mifepristone</a> (also known as RU-486) in the 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kapp2013_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kapp2013-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Creinin_2009_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Creinin_2009-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kapp_2009_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kapp_2009-61">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most common early first-trimester medical abortion regimens use mifepristone in combination with <a href="/wiki/Misoprostol" title="Misoprostol">misoprostol</a> (or sometimes another prostaglandin analog, <a href="/wiki/Gemeprost" title="Gemeprost">gemeprost</a>) up to 10 weeks (70 days) gestational age,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-63">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Methotrexate" title="Methotrexate">methotrexate</a> in combination with a prostaglandin analog up to 7 weeks gestation, or a prostaglandin analog alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[17]</a></sup> Mifepristone–misoprostol combination regimens work faster and are more effective at later gestational ages than methotrexate–misoprostol combination regimens, and combination regimens are more effective than misoprostol alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Creinin_2009_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Creinin_2009-60">[59]</a></sup> This regimen is effective in the second trimester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Medical abortion regimens involving mifepristone followed by misoprostol in the cheek between 24 and 48 hours later are effective when performed before 70 days' gestation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-63">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>In very early abortions, up to 7 weeks <a href="/wiki/Gestation" title="Gestation">gestation</a>, medical abortion using a mifepristone–misoprostol combination regimen is considered to be more effective than surgical abortion (<a href="/wiki/Vacuum_aspiration" title="Vacuum aspiration">vacuum aspiration</a>), especially when clinical practice does not include detailed inspection of aspirated tissue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_FAQs_2006_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_FAQs_2006-65">[64]</a></sup> Early medical abortion regimens using mifepristone, followed 24–48 hours later by buccal or vaginal misoprostol are 98% effective up to 9 weeks gestational age; from 9 to 10 weeks efficacy decreases modestly to 94%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fjerstad_2009b_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fjerstad_2009b-66">[65]</a></sup> If medical abortion fails, surgical abortion must be used to complete the procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early medical abortions account for the majority of abortions before 9 weeks gestation in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Great_Britain" title="Abortion in Great Britain">Britain</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_France" title="Abortion in France">France</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Switzerland" title="Abortion in Switzerland">Switzerland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_United_States" title="Abortion in the United States">United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>Medical abortion regimens using mifepristone in combination with a prostaglandin analog are the most common methods used for second-trimester abortions in <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Canada" title="Abortion in Canada">Canada</a>, most of Europe, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_China" title="Abortion in China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_India" title="Abortion in India">India</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kapp_2009_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kapp_2009-61">[60]</a></sup> in contrast to the United States where 96% of second-trimester abortions are performed surgically by <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_evacuation" title="Dilation and evacuation">dilation and evacuation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2020 Cochrane Systematic Review concluded that providing women with medications to take home to complete the second stage of the procedure for an early medical abortion results in an effective abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-75">[74]</a></sup> Further research is required to determine if self-administered medical abortion is as safe as provider-administered medical abortion, where a health care professional is present to help manage the medical abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-75">[74]</a></sup> Safely permitting women to self-administer abortion medication has the potential to improve access to abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-75">[74]</a></sup> Other research gaps that were identified include how to best support women who choose to take the medication home for a self-administered abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-:4-75">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surgical">Surgical</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vacuum-aspiration_(single).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg/220px-Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg/330px-Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg/440px-Vacuum-aspiration_%28single%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vacuum-aspiration_(single).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A vacuum aspiration abortion at eight weeks gestational age (six weeks after fertilization).<br/><b>1:</b> <a href="/wiki/Amniotic_sac" title="Amniotic sac">Amniotic sac</a><br/><b>2:</b> <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">Embryo</a><br/><b>3:</b> <a href="/wiki/Endometrium" title="Endometrium">Uterine lining</a><br/><b>4:</b> <a href="/wiki/Speculum_(medical)" title="Speculum (medical)">Speculum</a><br/><b>5:</b> Vacurette<br/><b>6:</b> Attached to a <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_pump" title="Vacuum pump">suction pump</a></div></div></div>
<p>Up to 15 weeks' gestation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suction-aspiration_abortion" title="Suction-aspiration abortion">suction-aspiration</a> or vacuum aspiration are the most common surgical methods of induced abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> <i>Manual vacuum aspiration</i> (MVA) consists of removing the <a href="/wiki/Fetus" title="Fetus">fetus</a> or <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Placenta" title="Placenta">placenta</a>, and membranes by suction using a manual syringe, while <i>electric vacuum aspiration</i> (EVA) uses an electric pump. These techniques can both be used very early in pregnancy. MVA can be used up to 14 weeks but is more often used earlier in the U.S. EVA can be used later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>MVA, also known as "mini-suction" and "<a href="/wiki/Menstrual_extraction" title="Menstrual extraction">menstrual extraction</a>" or EVA can be used in very early pregnancy when cervical dilation may not be required. <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_curettage" title="Dilation and curettage">Dilation and curettage</a> (D&amp;C) refers to opening the cervix (dilation) and removing tissue (curettage) via suction or sharp instruments. D&amp;C is a standard gynecological procedure performed for a variety of reasons, including examination of the uterine lining for possible malignancy, investigation of abnormal bleeding, and abortion. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> recommends <i>sharp curettage</i> only when suction aspiration is unavailable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_evacuation" title="Dilation and evacuation">Dilation and evacuation</a> (D&amp;E), used after 12 to 16 weeks, consists of opening the <a href="/wiki/Cervix" title="Cervix">cervix</a> and emptying the uterus using surgical instruments and suction. D&amp;E is performed vaginally and does not require an incision. <a href="/wiki/Intact_dilation_and_extraction" title="Intact dilation and extraction">Intact dilation and extraction</a> (D&amp;X) refers to a variant of D&amp;E sometimes used after 18 to 20 weeks when removal of an intact fetus improves surgical safety or for other reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>Abortion may also be performed surgically by hysterotomy or gravid hysterectomy. <a href="/wiki/Hysterotomy_abortion" title="Hysterotomy abortion">Hysterotomy abortion</a> is a procedure similar to a <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">caesarean section</a> and is performed under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_anesthesia" title="General anesthesia">general anesthesia</a>. It requires a smaller incision than a caesarean section and can be used during later stages of pregnancy. Gravid hysterectomy refers to removal of the whole uterus while still containing the pregnancy.  Hysterotomy and hysterectomy are associated with much higher rates of maternal morbidity and mortality than D&amp;E or induction abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>First-trimester procedures can generally be performed using <a href="/wiki/Local_anesthesia" title="Local anesthesia">local anesthesia</a>, while second-trimester methods may require <a href="/wiki/Sedation#Levels_of_sedation" title="Sedation">deep sedation</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_anesthesia" title="General anesthesia">general anesthesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEJMDec2011_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-NEJMDec2011-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_induction_abortion">Labor induction abortion</span></h3>
<p>In places lacking the necessary medical skill for dilation and extraction, or where preferred by practitioners, an abortion can be induced by first <a href="/wiki/Labor_induction" title="Labor induction">inducing labor</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Late_termination_of_pregnancy#Methods" title="Late termination of pregnancy">inducing fetal demise</a> if necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLOWM_Late_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-GLOWM_Late-83">[82]</a></sup> This is sometimes called "induced miscarriage". This procedure may be performed from 13 weeks gestation to the third trimester. Although it is very uncommon in the United States, more than 80% of induced abortions throughout the second trimester are labor-induced abortions in Sweden and other nearby countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Labor_Induced_Abortion-84">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Only limited data are available comparing this method with dilation and extraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Labor_Induced_Abortion-84">[83]</a></sup> Unlike D&amp;E, labor-induced abortions after 18 weeks may be complicated by the occurrence of brief fetal survival, which may be legally characterized as live birth. For this reason, labor-induced abortion is legally risky in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-Labor_Induced_Abortion-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAF_2015_Policy_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAF_2015_Policy-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_methods">Other methods</span></h3>
<p>Historically, a number of herbs reputed to possess abortifacient properties have been used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folk_medicine" title="Folk medicine">folk medicine</a>. Among these are: <a href="/wiki/Tansy" title="Tansy">tansy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mentha_pulegium" title="Mentha pulegium">pennyroyal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_cohosh" title="Black cohosh">black cohosh</a>, and the now-extinct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silphium_(antiquity)" title="Silphium (antiquity)">silphium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riddle2_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-riddle2-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 44–47, 62–63, 154–55, 230–31">: 44–47, 62–63, 154–55, 230–31 </span></sup>
</p><p>In 1978, one woman in Colorado died and another developed organ damage when they attempted to terminate their pregnancies by taking pennyroyal oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup>
Because the indiscriminant use of herbs as abortifacients can cause serious—even lethal—side effects, such as <a href="/wiki/Multiple_organ_dysfunction_syndrome" title="Multiple organ dysfunction syndrome">multiple organ failure</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> such use is not recommended by physicians.
</p><p>Abortion is sometimes attempted by causing trauma to the abdomen. The degree of force, if severe, can cause serious internal injuries without necessarily succeeding in inducing <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> In Southeast Asia, there is an ancient tradition of attempting abortion through forceful abdominal massage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-potts_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-potts-90">[89]</a></sup> One of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas_relief" title="Bas relief">bas reliefs</a> decorating the temple of <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> in Cambodia depicts a demon performing such an abortion upon a woman who has been sent to the <a href="/wiki/Underworld" title="Underworld">underworld</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-potts_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-potts-90">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Reported methods of unsafe, <a href="/wiki/Self-induced_abortion" title="Self-induced abortion">self-induced abortion</a> include misuse of <a href="/wiki/Misoprostol" title="Misoprostol">misoprostol</a> and insertion of non-surgical implements such as knitting needles and clothes hangers into the uterus. These and other methods to terminate pregnancy may be called "induced miscarriage".  Such methods are rarely used in countries where surgical abortion is legal and available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign,_Joe_Slovo_Park,_Cape_Town,_South_Africa-3869.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg/220px-Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg/330px-Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg/440px-Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign%2C_Joe_Slovo_Park%2C_Cape_Town%2C_South_Africa-3869.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abortion_Quick_%26_Pain_Free_sign,_Joe_Slovo_Park,_Cape_Town,_South_Africa-3869.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A likely illegal abortion flyer in South Africa</div></div></div>
<p>The health risks of abortion depend principally upon whether the procedure is performed safely or unsafely. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) defines <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">unsafe abortions</a> as those performed by unskilled individuals, with hazardous equipment, or in unsanitary facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who-unsafe-1992_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-who-unsafe-1992-92">[91]</a></sup> Legal abortions performed in the <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed world</a> are among the safest procedures in medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-grimes_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-lancet-grimes-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grimes-overview_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-grimes-overview-93">[92]</a></sup> In the United States as of 2012, abortion was estimated to be about 14 times safer for women than childbirth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimes2012_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grimes2012-12">[11]</a></sup> CDC estimated in 2019 that US pregnancy-related mortality was 17.2 maternal deaths per 100,000 live births,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> while the US abortion mortality rate is 0.7 maternal deaths per 100,000 procedures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ray2014_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ray2014-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> In the UK, guidelines of the Royal College of Obstetricians and Gynaecologists state that "Women should be advised that abortion is generally safer than continuing a pregnancy to term."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Worldwide, on average, abortion is safer than carrying a pregnancy to term. A 2007 study reported that "26% of all pregnancies worldwide are terminated by induced abortion," whereas "deaths from improperly performed [abortion] procedures constitute 13% of maternal mortality globally."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> In Indonesia in 2000 it was estimated that 2 million pregnancies ended in abortion, 4.5 million pregnancies were carried to term, and 14-16 percent of maternal deaths resulted from abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the US from 2000 to 2009, abortion had a mortality rate lower than <a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">plastic surgery</a>, lower or similar to running a marathon, and about equivalent to traveling 760 miles (1,220 km) in a passenger car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ray2014_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ray2014-11">[10]</a></sup> Five years after seeking abortion services, women who gave birth after being denied an abortion reported worse health than women who had either first or second trimester abortions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The risk of abortion-related mortality increases with gestational age, but remains lower than that of childbirth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Outpatient abortion is as safe from 64 to 70 days' gestation as it before 63 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is little difference in terms of safety and efficacy between medical abortion using a combined regimen of mifepristone and misoprostol and surgical abortion (vacuum aspiration) in early first trimester abortions up to 10 weeks gestation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_FAQs_2006_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_FAQs_2006-65">[64]</a></sup> Medical abortion using the prostaglandin analog misoprostol alone is less effective and more painful than medical abortion using a combined regimen of mifepristone and misoprostol or surgical abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vacuum_aspiration" title="Vacuum aspiration">Vacuum aspiration</a> in the first trimester is the safest method of surgical abortion, and can be performed in a <a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">primary care office</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_clinic" title="Abortion clinic">abortion clinic</a>, or hospital. Complications, which are rare, can include <a href="/wiki/Uterine_perforation" title="Uterine perforation">uterine perforation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endometritis" title="Endometritis">pelvic infection</a>, and retained products of conception requiring a second procedure to evacuate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arch-fam-practice_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-arch-fam-practice-104">[103]</a></sup> Infections account for one-third of abortion-related deaths in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> The rate of complications of vacuum aspiration abortion in the first trimester is similar regardless of whether the procedure is performed in a hospital, surgical center, or office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Preventive antibiotics (such as <a href="/wiki/Doxycycline" title="Doxycycline">doxycycline</a> or <a href="/wiki/Metronidazole" title="Metronidazole">metronidazole</a>) are typically given before abortion procedures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> as they are believed to substantially reduce the risk of postoperative uterine infection;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEJMDec2011_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-NEJMDec2011-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> however, antibiotics are not routinely given with abortion pills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The rate of failed procedures does not appear to vary significantly depending on whether the abortion is performed by a doctor or a <a href="/wiki/Mid-level_practitioner" title="Mid-level practitioner">mid-level practitioner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>Complications after second-trimester abortion are similar to those after first-trimester abortion, and depend somewhat on the method chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> The risk of death from abortion approaches roughly half the risk of death from childbirth the farther along a woman is in pregnancy; from one in a million before 9 weeks gestation to nearly one in ten thousand at 21 weeks or more (as measured from the last menstrual period).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bartlett2004_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett2004-113">[112]</a></sup> It appears that having had a prior surgical uterine evacuation (whether because of induced abortion or treatment of miscarriage) correlates with a small increase in the risk of preterm birth in future pregnancies. The studies supporting this did not control for factors not related to abortion or miscarriage, and hence the causes of this correlation have not been determined, although multiple possibilities have been suggested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saccone2016_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saccone2016-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some purported risks of abortion are promoted primarily by anti-abortion groups,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JASEN_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-JASEN-116">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cancer_Linacre_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cancer_Linacre-117">[116]</a></sup>
but lack scientific support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JASEN_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-JASEN-116">[115]</a></sup> For example, the question of a link between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abortion-breast_cancer_hypothesis" title="Abortion-breast cancer hypothesis">induced abortion and breast cancer</a> has been investigated extensively. Major medical and scientific bodies (including the WHO, <a href="/wiki/National_Cancer_Institute" title="National Cancer Institute">National Cancer Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Cancer_Society" title="American Cancer Society">American Cancer Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Obstetricians_and_Gynaecologists" title="Royal College of Obstetricians and Gynaecologists">Royal College of OBGYN</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Congress_of_Obstetricians_and_Gynecologists" title="American Congress of Obstetricians and Gynecologists">American Congress of OBGYN</a>) have concluded that abortion does not cause breast cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the past even illegality has not automatically meant that the abortions were unsafe. Referring to the U.S., historian <a href="/wiki/Linda_Gordon" title="Linda Gordon">Linda Gordon</a> states: "In fact, illegal abortions in this country have an impressive safety record."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 25">: 25 </span></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Rickie_Solinger" title="Rickie Solinger">Rickie Solinger</a>,
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>A related myth, promulgated by a broad spectrum of people concerned about abortion and public policy, is that before legalization abortionists were dirty and dangerous back-alley butchers.... [T]he historical evidence does not support such claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 4">: 4 </span></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Authors Jerome Bates and Edward Zawadzki describe the case of an illegal abortionist in the eastern U.S. in the early 20th century who was proud of having successfully completed 13,844 abortions without any fatality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 59">: 59 </span></sup>
In 1870s New York City the famous abortionist/midwife <a href="/wiki/Madame_Restell" title="Madame Restell">Madame Restell</a> (Anna Trow Lohman) appears to have lost very few women among her more than 100,000 patients<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup>—a lower mortality rate than the childbirth mortality rate at the time. In 1936, the prominent professor of obstetrics and gynecology <a href="/wiki/Frederick_J._Taussig" title="Frederick J. Taussig">Frederick J. Taussig</a> wrote that a cause of increasing mortality during the years of illegality in the U.S. was that
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>With each decade of the past fifty years the actual and proportionate frequency of this accident [perforation of the uterus] has increased, due, first, to the increase in the number of instrumentally induced abortions; second, to the proportionate increase in abortions handled by doctors as against those handled by midwives; and, third, to the prevailing tendency to use instruments instead of the finger in emptying the uterus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 223">: 223 </span></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health">Mental health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abortion_and_mental_health" title="Abortion and mental health">Abortion and mental health</a></div>
<p>Current evidence finds no relationship between most induced abortions and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_and_mental_health" title="Abortion and mental health">mental health problems</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2014_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2014-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hor2017_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hor2017-124">[123]</a></sup> other than those expected for any unwanted pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apa-press_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-apa-press-125">[124]</a></sup> A report by the <a href="/wiki/American_Psychological_Association" title="American Psychological Association">American Psychological Association</a> concluded that a woman's first abortion is not a threat to mental health when carried out in the first trimester, with such women no more likely to have mental-health problems than those carrying an unwanted pregnancy to term; the mental-health outcome of a woman's second or greater abortion is less certain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apa-press_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-apa-press-125">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> Some older reviews concluded that abortion was associated with an increased risk of psychological problems;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> however, they did not use an appropriate control group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hor2017_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hor2017-124">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although some studies show negative mental-health outcomes in women who choose abortions after the first trimester because of fetal abnormalities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apa-2008_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-apa-2008-128">[127]</a></sup> more rigorous research would be needed to show this conclusively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinberg2011_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steinberg2011-129">[128]</a></sup> Some proposed negative psychological effects of abortion have been referred to by anti-abortion advocates as a separate condition called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-abortion_syndrome" title="Post-abortion syndrome">post-abortion syndrome</a>", but this is not recognized by medical or psychological professionals in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2020 long term-study among US women found that about 99% of women felt that they made the right decision five years after they had an abortion. Relief was the primary emotion with few women feeling sadness or guilt. Social stigma was a main factor predicting negative emotions and regret years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unsafe_abortion">Unsafe abortion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">Unsafe abortion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RussianAbortionPoster.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1117" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/RussianAbortionPoster.jpg/220px-RussianAbortionPoster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/RussianAbortionPoster.jpg/330px-RussianAbortionPoster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/RussianAbortionPoster.jpg/440px-RussianAbortionPoster.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RussianAbortionPoster.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soviet poster circa 1925, warning against midwives performing abortions. Title translation: "Miscarriages induced by either grandma or self-taught midwives not only maim the woman, they also often lead to death."</div></div></div>
<p>Women seeking an abortion may use unsafe methods, especially when it is legally restricted. They may attempt <a href="/wiki/Self-induced_abortion" title="Self-induced abortion">self-induced abortion</a> or seek the help of a person without proper medical training or facilities. This can lead to severe complications, such as incomplete abortion, <a href="/wiki/Sepsis" title="Sepsis">sepsis</a>, hemorrhage, and damage to internal organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unsafe abortions are a major cause of injury and death among women worldwide. Although data are imprecise, it is estimated that approximately 20 million unsafe abortions are performed annually, with 97% taking place in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-grimes_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-lancet-grimes-10">[9]</a></sup> Unsafe abortions are believed to result in millions of injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-grimes_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-lancet-grimes-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haddad-2009_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haddad-2009-133">[132]</a></sup> Estimates of deaths vary according to methodology, and have ranged from 37,000 to 70,000 in the past decade;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-grimes_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-lancet-grimes-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBGY09_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-OBGY09-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loz2012_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Loz2012-134">[133]</a></sup> deaths from unsafe abortion account for around 13% of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_deaths" title="Maternal deaths">maternal deaths</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> believes that mortality has fallen since the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-136">[135]</a></sup> To reduce the number of unsafe abortions, public health organizations have generally advocated emphasizing the legalization of abortion, training of medical personnel, and ensuring access to reproductive-health services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berer-who_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-berer-who-137">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>A major factor in whether abortions are performed safely or not is the legal standing of abortion. Countries with restrictive abortion laws have higher rates of unsafe abortion and similar overall abortion rates compared to those where abortion is legal and available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBGY09_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-OBGY09-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berer-who_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-berer-who-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2007_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2007-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO-unsafe-2007_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-unsafe-2007-139">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (October 2021)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, the 1996 legalization of abortion in South Africa had an immediate positive impact on the frequency of abortion-related complications,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewkes_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-jewkes-142">[141]</a></sup> with abortion-related deaths dropping by more than 90%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bateman-samj_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-bateman-samj-143">[142]</a></sup> Similar reductions in maternal mortality have been observed after other countries have liberalized their abortion laws, such as <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> A 2011 study concluded that in the United States, some state-level anti-abortion laws are correlated with lower rates of abortion in that state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> The analysis, however, did not take into account travel to other states without such laws to obtain an abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> In addition, a lack of access to effective contraception contributes to unsafe abortion. It has been estimated that the incidence of unsafe abortion could be reduced by up to 75% (from 20 million to 5 million annually) if modern family planning and maternal health services were readily available globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singh-147">[146]</a></sup> Rates of such abortions may be difficult to measure because they can be reported variously as miscarriage, "induced miscarriage", "menstrual regulation", "mini-abortion", and "regulation of a delayed/suspended menstruation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pandemic_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pandemic-148">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brazil_Unsafe_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brazil_Unsafe-149">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>Forty percent of the world's women are able to access therapeutic and elective abortions within gestational limits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJGO10_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-IJGO10-29">[28]</a></sup> while an additional 35 percent have access to legal abortion if they meet certain physical, mental, or socioeconomic criteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dev98-07_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dev98-07-32">[31]</a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal mortality</a> seldom results from safe abortions, unsafe abortions result in 70,000 deaths and 5 million disabilities per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBGY09_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-OBGY09-22">[21]</a></sup> Complications of unsafe abortion account for approximately an eighth of maternal mortalities worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maclean_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maclean-150">[149]</a></sup> though this varies by region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> Secondary infertility caused by an unsafe abortion affects an estimated 24 million women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO-unsafe-2007_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-unsafe-2007-139">[138]</a></sup> The rate of unsafe abortions has increased from 44% to 49% between 1995 and 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup> Health education, access to family planning, and improvements in health care during and after abortion have been proposed to address this phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidence">Incidence</span></h2>
<p>There are two commonly used methods of measuring the incidence of abortion:
</p>
<ul><li>Abortion rate – number of abortions annually per 1,000 women between 15 and 44 years of age;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> some sources use a range of 15–49.</li>
<li>Abortion percentage – number of abortions out of 100 known pregnancies; pregnancies include live births, abortions, and miscarriages.</li></ul>
<p>In many places, where abortion is illegal or carries a heavy social stigma, medical reporting of abortion is not reliable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2007_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2007-138">[137]</a></sup> For this reason, estimates of the incidence of abortion must be made without determining certainty related to standard error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup> The number of abortions performed worldwide seems to have remained stable in recent years, with 41.6 million having been performed in 2003 and 43.8 million having been performed in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup> The abortion rate worldwide was 28 per 1000 women per year, though it was 24 per 1000 women per year for developed countries and 29 per 1000 women per year for developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-6"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup> The same 2012 study indicated that in 2008, the estimated abortion percentage of known pregnancies was at 21% worldwide, with 26% in developed countries and 20% in developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sedgh_2012_26-7"><a href="#cite_note-Sedgh_2012-26">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>On average, the incidence of abortion is similar in countries with restrictive abortion laws and those with more liberal access to abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes-abortion-rates_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-abortion-rates-154">[153]</a></sup> Restrictive abortion laws are associated with increases in the percentage of abortions performed unsafely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJGO10_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-IJGO10-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes-abortion-rates_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-abortion-rates-154">[153]</a></sup> The unsafe abortion rate in developing countries is partly attributable to lack of access to modern contraceptives; according to the <a href="/wiki/Guttmacher_Institute" title="Guttmacher Institute">Guttmacher Institute</a>, providing access to contraceptives would result in about 14.5 million fewer unsafe abortions and 38,000 fewer deaths from unsafe abortion annually worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The rate of legal, induced abortion varies extensively worldwide. According to the report of employees of Guttmacher Institute it ranged from 7 per 1000 women per year (Germany and Switzerland) to 30 per 1000 women per year (Estonia) in countries with complete statistics in 2008. The proportion of pregnancies that ended in induced abortion ranged from about 10% (Israel, the Netherlands and Switzerland) to 30% (Estonia) in the same group, though it might be as high as 36% in Hungary and Romania, whose statistics were deemed incomplete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>An American study in 2002 concluded that about half of women having abortions were using a form of <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">contraception</a> at the time of becoming pregnant. Inconsistent use was reported by half of those using <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condoms</a> and three-quarters of those using the <a href="/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Combined oral contraceptive pill">birth control pill</a>; 42% of those using condoms reported failure through slipping or breakage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> The Guttmacher Institute estimated that "most abortions in the United States are obtained by minority women" because minority women "have much higher rates of unintended pregnancy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> In a 2022 analysis by the <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Family_Foundation" title="Kaiser Family Foundation">Kaiser Family Foundation</a>, while people of color comprise 44% of the population in Mississippi, 59% of the population in Texas, 42% of the population in Louisiana (by the state Health Department), and 35% of the population in Alabama, they comprise 80%, 74%, 72%, and 70% of those receiving abortions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p>The abortion rate may also be expressed as the average number of abortions a woman has during her reproductive years; this is referred to as <i>total abortion rate</i> (TAR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gestational_age_and_method">Gestational age and method</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="405" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg/200px-UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg/300px-UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg/400px-UK_abortion_by_gestational_age_2019_histogram.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="405" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg/200px-US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg/300px-US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg/400px-US_abortion_by_gestational_age_2016_histogram.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Histogram" title="Histogram">Histogram</a> of abortions by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestational_age_(obstetrics)" title="Gestational age (obstetrics)">gestational age</a> in England and Wales during 2019 (left). Abortion in the United States by gestational age, 2016 (right).</div></div></div></div>
<p>Abortion rates also vary depending on the stage of pregnancy and the method practiced. In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC) reported that 26% of reported legal induced abortions in the United States were known to have been obtained at less than 6 weeks' gestation, 18% at 7 weeks, 15% at 8 weeks, 18% at 9 through 10 weeks, 10% at 11 through 12 weeks, 6% at 13 through 15 weeks, 4% at 16 through 20 weeks and 1% at more than 21 weeks. 91% of these were classified as having been done by "<a href="/wiki/Curettage" title="Curettage">curettage</a>" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suction-aspiration_abortion" title="Suction-aspiration abortion">suction-aspiration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_curettage" title="Dilation and curettage">dilation and curettage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_evacuation" title="Dilation and evacuation">dilation and evacuation</a>), 8% by "<a href="/wiki/Medical_abortion" title="Medical abortion">medical</a>" means (<a href="/wiki/Mifepristone" title="Mifepristone">mifepristone</a>), &gt;1% by "<a href="/wiki/Instillation_abortion" title="Instillation abortion">intrauterine instillation</a>" (saline or <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin" title="Prostaglandin">prostaglandin</a>), and 1% by "other" (including <a href="/wiki/Hysterotomy_abortion" title="Hysterotomy abortion">hysterotomy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hysterectomy" title="Hysterectomy">hysterectomy</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdc2003_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdc2003-163">[162]</a></sup> According to the CDC, due to data collection difficulties the data must be viewed as tentative and some fetal deaths reported beyond 20 weeks may be natural deaths erroneously classified as abortions if the removal of the dead fetus is accomplished by the same procedure as an induced abortion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guttmacher_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-guttmacher-7">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Guttmacher Institute estimated there were 2,200 <a href="/wiki/Intact_dilation_and_extraction" title="Intact dilation and extraction">intact dilation and extraction</a> procedures in the US during 2000; this accounts for &lt;0.2% of the total number of abortions performed that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> Similarly, in England and Wales in 2006, 89% of terminations occurred at or under 12 weeks, 9% between 13 and 19 weeks, and 2% at or over 20 weeks. 64% of those reported were by vacuum aspiration, 6% by D&amp;E, and 30% were medical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> There are more second trimester abortions in developing countries such as China, India and Vietnam than in developed countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motivation">Motivation</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal">Personal</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="898" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png/400px-AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png/600px-AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png/800px-AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AGIAbortionReasonsBarChart.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A bar chart depicting selected data from a 1998 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Guttmacher_Institute" title="Alan Guttmacher Institute">AGI</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meta-study" title="Meta-study">meta-study</a> on the reasons women stated for having an abortion.</div></div></div>
