<li id="cite_note-Labor_Induced_Abortion-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Labor_Induced_Abortion_84-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFBorgattaKapp2011">Borgatta L, Kapp N (July 2011). <a class="external text" href="http://www.contraceptionjournal.org/article/S0010-7824(11)00057-6/pdf" rel="nofollow">"Clinical guidelines. Labor induction abortion in the second trimester"</a>. <i>Contraception</i>. <b>84</b> (1): 4–18. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.contraception.2011.02.005" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.contraception.2011.02.005</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/21664506" rel="nofollow">21664506</a>. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200606205318/https://www.contraceptionjournal.org/article/S0010-7824(11)00057-6/pdf" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 6 June 2020<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">25 September</span> 2015</span>. <q>10. What is the effect of feticide on labor induction abortion outcome? Deliberately causing demise of the fetus before labor induction abortion is performed primarily to avoid transient fetal survival after expulsion; this approach may be for the comfort of both the woman and the staff, to avoid futile resuscitation efforts. Some providers allege that feticide also facilitates delivery, although little data support this claim. Transient fetal survival is very unlikely after intraamniotic installation of saline or urea, which are directly feticidal. Transient survival with misoprostol for labor induction abortion at greater than 18 weeks ranges from 0% to 50% and has been observed in up to 13% of abortions performed with high-dose oxytocin. Factors associated with a higher likelihood of transient fetal survival with labor induction abortion include increasing gestational age, decreasing abortion interval and the use of nonfeticidal inductive agents such as the PGE1 analogues.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Contraception&amp;rft.atitle=Clinical+guidelines.+Labor+induction+abortion+in+the+second+trimester&amp;rft.volume=84&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=4-18&amp;rft.date=2011-07&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.contraception.2011.02.005&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F21664506&amp;rft.aulast=Borgatta&amp;rft.aufirst=L&amp;rft.au=Kapp%2C+N&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.contraceptionjournal.org%2Farticle%2FS0010-7824%2811%2900057-6%2Fpdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-NAF_2015_Policy-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NAF_2015_Policy_85-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://prochoice.org/wp-content/uploads/2015_NAF_CPGs.pdf" rel="nofollow"><i>2015 Clinical Policy Guidelines</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. National Abortion Federation. 2015. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150812220053/http://prochoice.org/wp-content/uploads/2015_NAF_CPGs.pdf" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on 12 August 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">30 October</span> 2015</span>. <q>Policy Statement: Medical induction abortion is a safe and effective method for termination of pregnancies beyond the first trimester when performed by trained clinicians in medical offices, freestanding clinics, ambulatory surgery centers, and hospitals. Feticidal agents may be particularly important when issues of viability arise.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=2015+Clinical+Policy+Guidelines&amp;rft.pub=National+Abortion+Federation&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fprochoice.org%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2015_NAF_CPGs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSteinauerJacksonGrossman2013">Steinauer J, Jackson A, Grossman D,  et al. <li id="cite_note-JASEN-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-JASEN_116-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-JASEN_116-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFJasen2005">Jasen P (October 2005). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1251638" rel="nofollow">"Breast cancer and the politics of abortion in the United States"</a>. <i>Medical History</i>. <b>49</b> (4): 423–444. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1017%2FS0025727300009145" rel="nofollow">10.1017/S0025727300009145</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1251638" rel="nofollow">1251638</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16562329" rel="nofollow">16562329</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Medical+History&amp;rft.atitle=Breast+cancer+and+the+politics+of+abortion+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.volume=49&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=423-444&amp;rft.date=2005-10&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC1251638%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F16562329&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2FS0025727300009145&amp;rft.aulast=Jasen&amp;rft.aufirst=P&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC1251638&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Cancer_Linacre-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cancer_Linacre_117-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSchneiderZainerKubatMullen2014">Schneider AP, Zainer CM, Kubat CK, Mullen NK, Windisch AK (August 2014). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4135458" rel="nofollow">"The breast cancer epidemic: 10 facts"</a>. <i>The Linacre Quarterly</i>. Catholic Medical Association. <b>81</b> (3): 244–277. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1179%2F2050854914Y.0000000027" rel="nofollow">10.1179/2050854914Y.0000000027</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4135458" rel="nofollow">4135458</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/25249706" rel="nofollow">25249706</a>. <q>an association between [induced abortion] and breast cancer has been found by numerous Western and non-Western researchers from around the world. This is especially true in more recent reports that allow for a sufficient breast cancer latency period since an adoption of a Western life style in sexual and reproductive behavior.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Linacre+Quarterly&amp;rft.atitle=The+breast+cancer+epidemic%3A+10+facts&amp;rft.volume=81&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=244-277&amp;rft.date=2014-08&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4135458%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F25249706&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1179%2F2050854914Y.0000000027&amp;rft.aulast=Schneider&amp;rft.aufirst=AP&amp;rft.au=Zainer%2C+CM&amp;rft.au=Kubat%2C+CK&amp;rft.au=Mullen%2C+NK&amp;rft.au=Windisch%2C+AK&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4135458&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFShahAhman2009">Shah I, Ahman E (December 2009). "Unsafe abortion: global and regional incidence, trends, consequences, and challenges". <i>Journal of Obstetrics and Gynaecology Canada</i>. <b>31</b> (12): 1149–1158. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fs1701-2163%2816%2934376-6" rel="nofollow">10.1016/s1701-2163(16)34376-6</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/20085681" rel="nofollow">20085681</a>. <q>However, a woman's chance of having an abortion is similar whether she lives in a developed or a developing region: in 2003 the rates were 26 abortions per 1,000 women aged 15 to 44 in developed areas and 29 per 1,000 in developing areas. The main difference is in safety, with abortion being safe and easily accessible in developed countries and generally restricted and unsafe in most developing countries.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Obstetrics+and+Gynaecology+Canada&amp;rft.atitle=Unsafe+abortion%3A+global+and+regional+incidence%2C+trends%2C+consequences%2C+and+challenges&amp;rft.volume=31&amp;rft.issue=12&amp;rft.pages=1149-1158&amp;rft.date=2009-12&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fs1701-2163%2816%2934376-6&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F20085681&amp;rft.aulast=Shah&amp;rft.aufirst=I&amp;rft.au=Ahman%2C+E&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-204"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-204">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFReagan2022">Reagan LJ (2022) [1997]. <i>When Abortion Was a Crime: Women, Medicine and the Law in the United States, 1867–1973</i> (1st ed.). Berkeley: University of California Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0520387416" title="Special:BookSources/978-0520387416"><bdi>978-0520387416</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=When+Abortion+Was+a+Crime%3A+Women%2C+Medicine+and+the+Law+in+the+United+States%2C+1867%E2%80%931973&amp;rft.place=Berkeley&amp;rft.edition=1st&amp;rft.pub=University+of+California+Press&amp;rft.date=2022&amp;rft.isbn=978-0520387416&amp;rft.aulast=Reagan&amp;rft.aufirst=LJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-205"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-205">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFBlakemore2022">Blakemore E (22 May 2022). <a class="external text" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/article/the-complex-early-history-of-abortion-in-the-united-states" rel="nofollow">"The complex early history of abortion in the United States"</a>. <i>National Geographic</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">26 July</span> 2022</span>. <q>But that view of history is the subject of great dispute. Though interpretations differ, most scholars who have investigated the history of abortion argue that terminating a pregnancy wasn't always illegal—or even controversial.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=National+Geographic&amp;rft.atitle=The+complex+early+history+of+abortion+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.date=2022-05-22&amp;rft.aulast=Blakemore&amp;rft.aufirst=E&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nationalgeographic.com%2Fhistory%2Farticle%2Fthe-complex-early-history-of-abortion-in-the-united-states&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Hardin_1978-206"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Hardin_1978_206-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hardin_1978_206-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hardin_1978_206-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFHardin1978">Hardin G (December 1978). "Abortion in America. The Origins and Evolution of National Policy, 1800–1900. James C. Mohr". <i>The Quarterly Review of Biology</i>. <b>53</b> (4): 499. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1086%2F410954" rel="nofollow">10.1086/410954</a>. <q>The long silence had led us to assume that opposition to abortion had existed from time immemorial. Not so: most of the opposition to, and all of the laws against, abortion arose in the 19th century. Historian Mohr amply documents the earlier acceptance of abortion. ... In the 19th century even many of the feminists expressed horror at abortion, urging abstinence instead. Not so in the 20th century. In the 19th century the medical profession was fairly united against abortion; Mohr argues that this arose from the commericial competition between the 'regulars' (men with M.D.'s) and the irregulars (women without M.D.'s). ... A key role in generating prohibition laws was played by the press, ... . By 1900 the abortion-prohibition laws were immune to questioning, as they remained until the 1960's when feminists and a new breed of physicians combined to arouse the public to the injustice of the law. ... the <i>Roe v. Wade</i> decision of the Supreme Court ... essentially returned the practice of abortion to the permissive state <i>ante</i> 1820.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Quarterly+Review+of+Biology&amp;rft.atitle=Abortion+in+America.+The+Origins+and+Evolution+of+National+Policy%2C+1800%E2%80%931900.+James+C.+Mohr&amp;rft.volume=53&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=499&amp;rft.date=1978-12&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1086%2F410954&amp;rft.aulast=Hardin&amp;rft.aufirst=G&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-207"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-207">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFAcevedo1979">Acevedo ZP (Summer 1979). "Abortion in early America". <i>Women Health</i>. <b>4</b> (2): 159–167. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1300%2FJ013v04n02_05" rel="nofollow">10.1300/J013v04n02_05</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/10297561" rel="nofollow">10297561</a>. <q>This piece describes abortion practices in use from the 1600s to the 19th century among the inhabitants of North America. The abortive techniques of women from different ethnic and racial groups as found in historical literature are revealed. Thus, the point is made that abortion is not simply a 'now issue' that effects select women. Instead, it is demonstrated that it is a widespread practice as solidly rooted in our past as it is in the present.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Women+Health&amp;rft.atitle=Abortion+in+early+America&amp;rft.ssn=summer&amp;rft.volume=4&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=159-167&amp;rft.date=1979&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1300%2FJ013v04n02_05&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F10297561&amp;rft.aulast=Acevedo&amp;rft.aufirst=ZP&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Alford_2003-208"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Alford_2003_208-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Alford_2003_208-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Alford_2003_208-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFAlford2003">Alford S (2003). <li id="cite_note-nations1977-238"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nations1977_238-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFNationsMisagoFonsecaCorreia1997">Nations MK, Misago C, Fonseca W, Correia LL, Campbell OM (June 1997). "Women's hidden transcripts about abortion in Brazil". <i>Social Science &amp; Medicine</i>. <b>44</b> (12): 1833–1845. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fs0277-9536%2896%2900293-6" rel="nofollow">10.1016/s0277-9536(96)00293-6</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/9194245" rel="nofollow">9194245</a>. <q>Two folk medical conditions, "delayed" (atrasada) and "suspended" (suspendida) menstruation, are described as perceived by poor Brazilian women in Northeast Brazil. Culturally prescribed methods to "regulate" these conditions and provoke menstrual bleeding are also described ...</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Science+%26+Medicine&amp;rft.atitle=Women%27s+hidden+transcripts+about+abortion+in+Brazil&amp;rft.volume=44&amp;rft.issue=12&amp;rft.pages=1833-1845&amp;rft.date=1997-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fs0277-9536%2896%2900293-6&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F9194245&amp;rft.aulast=Nations&amp;rft.aufirst=MK&amp;rft.au=Misago%2C+C&amp;rft.au=Fonseca%2C+W&amp;rft.au=Correia%2C+LL&amp;rft.au=Campbell%2C+OM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAbortion"></span></span>
